- **Survey-gated certificate auto-issue — Phase 2 (June 25, 2026, pkg 0.4.10→0.4.11)** — Completing the event survey now **auto-issues** every cert template flagged for it that the person qualifies for — **fully automatic** (rendered + emailed, no operator click; confirmed decision). The survey POST path is **untouched** (it already sets `surveyCompletedAt`); the cert worker drives off it. **Config (per template):** `CertificateTemplate.autoIssueOnSurvey` + `autoIssueTag` (editor toggle + tag input; REST POST/PATCH + MCP `create_/update_certificate_template`). A tag is **required** to match anyone (we refuse to mass-issue to everyone who surveyed); a flagged-but-tagless template is flagged in the analytics card + a `cert-auto-issue:template-missing-tag` warn. **Trigger = worker sweep** (no inline enqueue): new nullable `Registration.certAutoIssueCheckedAt` + a **partial index** (`WHERE certAutoIssueCheckedAt IS NULL AND surveyCompletedAt IS NOT NULL`); [src/lib/certificates/auto-issue.ts](src/lib/certificates/auto-issue.ts) `runAutoIssueSweep()` scans survey-completed-but-unchecked rows past their backoff gate. **Routing (constraint C):** attendee tags → **ATTENDANCE** templates → cert on `registrationId`; the linked speaker's tags (companion `sourceRegistrationId` reverse, else read-time email match) → **APPRECIATION** → cert on `speakerId` — a speaker who surveys via their companion gets **both**. Pure `selectAutoIssueTargets` (unit-tested). **Delivery reuses `CertificateIssueRun`** — each (template, recipient) → a 1-item run with a new `autoIssue` flag + **null operator** (nullable `CertificateIssueRun.triggeredByUserId` + `IssuedCertificate.issuedByUserId`); auto runs **skip the AWAITING_REVIEW gate** ([issue-worker.ts](src/lib/certificates/issue-worker.ts) render → SENDING directly). Whole per-registration resolve+enqueue+stamp is one transaction (crash-safe). **Idempotency:** per-template `IssuedCertificate` uniqueness **+** a pre-create guard (skip if a cert OR an auto-run item already covers (event, template, recipient)) — re-sweeps / crash-retries / manual-first can't duplicate or double-email. **Retry + backoff (operator-requested):** a transient per-reg failure bumps `certAutoIssueAttempts`, records `certAutoIssueError`, defers via `certAutoIssueNextAttemptAt = now + backoff` (1/5/15/60/180 min — never head-of-line-blocks the queue); after **5** attempts gives up terminally (manual Issue is the backstop). **Analytics (operator-requested):** every sweep logs `cert-auto-issue:sweep` with counts; `GET .../certificates/auto-issue/analytics` (registration state pending/retrying/resolved/gaveUp + auto-run delivery by status + certs-auto-issued + recent errors + tagless flag) surfaced as [AutoIssueAnalyticsCard](src/components/certificates/auto-issue-analytics-card.tsx) on the certificates page "Issue" tab (polls 20s). Sweep is folded into the **cert-issue** worker job (every 3 min: sweep → enqueue → `tickAllRuns()` drains) + mirrored on the legacy `/api/cron/certificate-issues` route. Migration `20260625160000_cert_survey_auto_issue` (all additive/nullable/idempotent — two NOT-NULL drops on issuer cols are blue-green safe). **Known limit:** a registration is swept once (`certAutoIssueCheckedAt` stamp); flagging a template auto-issue **after** someone surveyed needs **manual Issue** to cover them — flag before surveys go out. +12 tests (suite 1651). **Verify on prod:** flag a template + tag, complete a test survey for a tagged reg, confirm the cert renders+emails within minutes + the card reflects it.

event.cmeHours` (per-template override) + a new `{{role}}` token; REST POST/PATCH + MCP `create_/update_certificate_template` accept `role`/`cmeHours`; Role + CME-hours inputs in the template editor (CME hours entered manually per template; issuance stays tag-driven). **Phases 2–3 (planned):** survey-completion auto-issue (enqueue → existing cert worker; works for speakers now via their companion), manual override (mostly exists). - **Registration "open/closed" master toggle now enforced + branded closed page (June 24, 2026)** — The Settings → Registration **"Registration Open"** switch (`Event.settings.registrationOpen`) already existed and saved, but was a **no-op** — nothing on the public side read it. Wiring: the public event API ([public/events/[slug]/route.ts](src/app/api/public/events/%5Bslug%5D/route.ts)) now exposes `registrationOpen` (default **true** when the field is absent, so existing events aren't accidentally closed); the smart-redirect page ([e/[slug]/register/page.tsx](src/app/e/%5Bslug%5D/register/page.tsx)) skips the tier redirect and renders the **branded** "Registration Closed" page (event banner + info strip + a disabled "Registration Closed" CTA — previously this closed state was an unbranded bare card); the category page ([e/[slug]/register/[category]/page.tsx](src/app/e/%5Bslug%5D/register/%5Bcategory%5D/page.tsx)) folds the switch into `isClosed` (closed card + disabled CTA). **Server-side enforcement (defense in depth):** `POST /api/public/events/[slug]/register` now returns **403 `REGISTRATION_CLOSED`** when the switch is off, so a direct POST can't bypass the closed UI; the event `select` adds `settings`, the guard logs `public/register:registration-closed`. **Admin "Add Registration" (dashboard) is unaffected** — staff can still register people while public registration is closed (the switch governs only the public self-service flow). - **Zoom embed React-19 crash fixed via CDN loader (June 23, 2026, producer-reported)** — A live webinar showed *"Couldn't load the embedded meeting / Cannot read properties of undefined (reading 'ReactCurrentOwner')"*. **Root cause:** `@zoom/meetingsdk@6.0.0`'s `/embedded` UMD does **not** inline React — it externalizes `require("react")`/`require("react-dom")` and reads React-18's internal `ReactCurrentOwner`, which **React 19 removed**. The bundler resolved those externals to the app's React 19 → crash. (The long-standing note claiming "the SDK's bundled React 18 is isolated" was **wrong** for this version; corrected in memory.) **Fix:** new [src/lib/zoom/load-embedded-sdk.ts](src/lib/zoom/load-embedded-sdk.ts) `loadZoomMtgEmbedded()` loads the SDK + its **own React 18** from `source.zoom.us` (CDN) as isolated browser globals (`window.React`=18, `window.ZoomMtgEmbedded`) — Zoom's documented React-app integration, not a hack. The Next app keeps importing React 19 via the module graph, so they never collide. [ZoomWebEmbed](src/components/zoom/zoom-web-embed.tsx) now calls the loader at both mount + cleanup (same `ZoomMtgEmbedded` API, lifecycle unchanged). **Switchable** via `NEXT_PUBLIC_ZOOM_EMBED_LOADER`: `"cdn"` (default, works under React 19) vs `"npm"` (the bundled `import "@zoom/meetingsdk/embedded"` path — kept so we can flip back with **one env var, no code change** the moment Zoom ships a React-19-compatible SDK). CDN v6.0.0 URLs (react/react-dom/redux/redux-thunk/lodash vendor scripts + `zoom-meeting-embedded-6.0.0.min.js`) verified 200 + React 18.2.0. No app-level CSP blocks them (only `frame-ancestors 'self'`). tsc/eslint/vitest 1618/build green — **runtime join is best verified on prod after deploy** (a real meeting + signature is needed). Client View remains unsupported.

Pushed `4b29784` (fixes) + `2c53ca4` (poster); tsc/eslint/vitest 1618/build green; **takes effect on web deploy.** **(1) Attendee "Join Webinar" email CTA went straight to Zoom** — bypassing our gated session page + producer-controlled waiting room. Countdown + lobby message always render below. Docs: [docs/WEBINAR_EVENTS.md](docs/WEBINAR_EVENTS.md) (email join-URL note, attendee join path, three-tier lobby fallback).

- **Multi-tenant readiness audit (Round 2) + remediation (June 23, 2026)** — Ahead of white-label/multi-tenant work, a 3-agent adversarial audit (lenses: cross-tenant IDOR/org-scoping · RBAC/finance/auth · data-integrity/races/silent-failures) swept the API surface; findings logged as **Round 2** in [docs/PRODUCTION_AUDIT.md](docs/PRODUCTION_AUDIT.md) (#55–68: 0 BLOCKER, 5 HIGH, 5 MED, 4 LOW). All remediated in **3 verified batches** (each tsc/eslint/vitest/build clean), pushed to `main`: **batch 1 HIGH `bfc7596`**, **batch 2 MED/LOW `ce8737b`**, **batch 3 DATA-5 `09dab42`**, doc `a769238`. **Fixes:** **IDOR-1** promo-code GET ([promo-codes/[promoCodeId]/route.ts](src/app/api/events/%5BeventId%5D/promo-codes/%5BpromoCodeId%5D/route.ts)) now org-binds the event before exposing config + redemption PII (the PUT/DELETE already did). **RBAC-1** both `bulk-tags` PATCH routes (registrations + speakers) now call `denyReviewer` — they were the **only** event-scoped admin writes missing it (restricted roles could rewrite tags, which drive email cohorts + cert eligibility). **DATA-1** promo `usedCount` is released on registration cancel/delete (REST PUT+DELETE, MCP `update_registration` + `bulk_update_registration_status`) so a limited-use code isn't permanently exhausted after cancellations. **DATA-2/3/4** overbooking + reactivate/type-change oversell + CSV/EventsAir import races all converted from read-then-write to **atomic `updateMany` predicate guards** (`bookedRooms < totalRooms` / `soldCount < quantity`, `count===0 → error`) — the pattern `soldCount` create paths already used; the false-"atomic" comment in [accommodation-service.ts](src/services/accommodation-service.ts) is gone. **DATA-6** registration DELETE guards a possibly-shared Attendee with a sibling-count check before deleting. **DATA-5** new **`invoice-reconciliation`** worker job ([src/lib/invoice-reconciliation-worker.ts](src/lib/invoice-reconciliation-worker.ts), 10-min, advisory-lock 1006, +5 tests) recovers PAID registrations whose post-payment invoice the Stripe webhook's detached block dropped (PAID + PAID `Payment` + no `INVOICE` → re-run `createPaidInvoice`+`sendInvoiceEmail`; idempotent, 25/tick, 14-day look-back) — **needs worker redeploy to run**. **FIN-1** added `totalPrice` to `FINANCIAL_KEYS` + accommodation/hotel GET redact prices for non-finance roles (defense-in-depth — moot under the June-17 finance model where MEMBER/ONSITE are finance-capable and other roles are org-null, but future-proofs the new-roles direction). Two LOW catches now log instead of swallowing. **Two findings were FALSE POSITIVES** (verified against source, recorded in the doc): #56 IDOR-2 accommodation roomType wasn't exploitable (pre-tx validation already binds the event — hardened anyway), and #66 import-contacts already increments soldCount. Verified each batch: tsc 0, eslint 0, vitest 1618, build 0. **Code-only — not yet deployed.**

- **Webinar waiting room — producer-gated admission, holding video, per-event viewing mode, real-time presence, 5k CDN wiring (June 23, 2026)** — The webinar attendee live-day flow is now producer-controlled and watched **on our gated session page** (no BigMarker). **Phases 1–4 + a two-agent adversarial review** (commits `9229409`, `89d9c83`, then review fixes `ebf766b` / `9cdac92` / `517e1d4`; docs `f09fe30`). **(1) Lobby config + producer "Open the room"** — `WebinarSettings` ([src/lib/webinar.ts](src/lib/webinar.ts)) gained `viewingMode` (`"zoom"` embed vs `"hls"` custom stream), `lobbyVideoUrl` (YouTube/Vimeo holding video — host-allowlisted by [src/lib/webinar/lobby-video.ts](src/lib/webinar/lobby-video.ts), only `youtube-nocookie.com`/`player.vimeo.com` embeds, no arbitrary iframe), `lobbyMessage`; all in `Event.settings.webinar` JSON (no schema change). New **`POST /api/events/[eventId]/webinar/room`** `{open}` sets the **anchor `EventSession.status`** → `LIVE`/`COMPLETED` (the room-open source of truth — re-openable). Console **LobbyCard** ([webinar/page.tsx](src/app/(dashboard)/events/%5BeventId%5D/webinar/page.tsx)) has the mode toggle, video URL, message, and the **"Open the room / Go live" ↔ "Close the room"** button + `Room OPEN/closed` badge. **(2) Waiting room** — new [src/components/webinar/waiting-room.tsx](src/components/webinar/waiting-room.tsx) (countdown + looped holding video + message), shown when `eventType===WEBINAR` + a confirmed registrant + room not open + `!isPast`. New **public, cached** `GET .../sessions/[sessionId]/lobby-status` (single query session→event, **3s per-container micro-cache** so 5k pollers collapse to ~1 DB hit/3s; DRAFT events auto-open). The session page ([e/[slug]/session/[sessionId]/page.tsx](src/app/e/%5Bslug%5D/session/%5BsessionId%5D/page.tsx)) polls it (~15–20s jittered) and on `roomOpen` **re-mints** join creds (a page-load signature is likely expired after a long lobby wait) then auto-mounts the embed (`zoom`) or `LivePlayer` (`hls`), with a "Join now" CTA fallback; the admit latch resets on close (re-open re-admits) and on failed re-fetch (retry); the HLS view stays mounted past the scheduled end while the room is open (overrun). **(3) Real-time presence** — new **`WebinarPresence`** table (migration `20260623000000_add_webinar_presence`, additive/blue-green-safe) + write-once `Registration.webinarFirstJoinedAt`. **`POST .../sessions/[sessionId]/presence`** heartbeat (auth + registration-gated, org staff skipped) is an **`upsert`** (INSERT…ON CONFLICT, NO interactive transaction — two-tab first-beats can't P2002, no held connection at 5k), escalate-lobby→joined-only; client beats ~30–40s, paused when hidden. **`GET /api/events/[eventId]/webinar/presence`** (org-scoped) → who's present in the last 60s split lobby/joined → console **"Live now"** card; **"Joined"** badge on the registrations list. This is OUR-page presence, **distinct from post-event `ZoomAttendance`**. **(4) 5k stream** — HLS playback is CDN-aware via `HLS_CDN_BASE` (CloudFront) with app-origin fallback (in `stream-status` + `zoom-join`); `stream-status` keeps probing the MediaMTX origin (cached 3s so 5k pollers share one probe); `LivePlayer` fails over CDN→origin once then resumes the recovery poll (auto-reconnect, not a dead-end); nginx `/stream/` origin proxy committed to [deploy/nginx.conf](deploy/nginx.conf); operator-run CloudFront + Singapore-DR failover steps in [docs/LIVE_STREAMING.md §13](docs/LIVE_STREAMING.md). Docs: [docs/WEBINAR_EVENTS.md](docs/WEBINAR_EVENTS.md) "Waiting room…" section + user-guide S11 live-day flow. **Deferred (in [docs/ROADMAP.md](docs/ROADMAP.md) backlog):** never-opened-room warning (decision: keep manual-open), operator visibility (DRAFT auto-open vs PUBLISHED), save-time hls/stream validation, `lobby-status` eventType gate, stale-badge, Redis rate limiter. **Operator prerequisites:** Zoom **Active SDK Mode dev→Production** + add the prod domain to the Marketplace embed allowlist (for the embed mode); verify the box's nginx `/stream/`; provision CloudFront+DR before a real 5k stream. - **Team invite: "set password now" mode (no email) for temp accounts (June 17, 2026)** — The Settings → Users invite was **email-only**: it created the account with a random throwaway password and emailed an `/accept-invitation` setup link, so the *user* set their own password by clicking it. For **temp accounts** on non-mailbox addresses (`@meetingmindsexperts.com` / `@meetingmindsgroup.com` — see internal-domain rule above) the email goes nowhere, so they could never log in (the gap an operator hit). The invite dialog now offers two **Account setup** modes (new users only): **(a) Send email invite** — unchanged; **(b) Set password now** — the admin types a password; the account is created **active + `emailVerified`** with that password and **NO email/token**, and the admin hands over the email+password for immediate sign-in. **Backend** ([organization/users/route.ts](src/app/api/organization/users/route.ts)): `POST` accepts an optional `password` (min 8); when present **and the email is new** (the promote branch still wins for an existing account) it creates the user directly (bcrypt hash, `emailVerified: now`), audits `CREATE_USER` with `mode: "password"`, logs `organization/users:created-with-password`, and returns `passwordSet: true` (201). When absent, the normal email-invitation flow runs. **Frontend** ([settings/page.tsx](src/app/%28dashboard%29/settings/page.tsx)): the mode toggle + a (plain-text, copyable) password field + a `passwordSet` success toast; submit button reads "Create Account" in password mode. **Scope:** new accounts only — resetting an existing account's password is a separate flow (not built). Verified: tsc 0, eslint 0, vitest 1583/1583, build 0. Commit `b27329d`.

- **ONSITE registration-desk role + internal-domain org membership + promote-on-invite (June 16, 2026)** — A new org-bound **Onsite Staff** role for the registration desk, plus the identity-model changes that make it usable for internal people who first signed up as attendees. **(1) ONSITE role** (`2dbe811`) — see the RBAC section above for the full enforcement matrix. Org-bound; can ONLY add a registration, check attendees in (~~+undo~~ — **undo was never implemented**, see the RBAC section), view the registrations list, and print badges; money hidden (like MEMBER — **also since corrected: MEMBER/ONSITE are finance-capable**). `denyReviewer` gained an `{ allow }` list so the create/check-in/badge routes opt ONSITE back in while the other 27 write routes block it; middleware ([src/proxy.ts](src/proxy.ts)) confines ONSITE to `/events` + an event's `/registrations*`+`/check-in*`; sidebar/header/list/detail-sheet all gate accordingly. Additive enum migration `20260616120000_add_onsite_role`. **(2) Invite "already exists" no longer silent** (`257c5fa`) — `POST /api/organization/users` returned a bare 400 with no log when the email matched a non-team account; it now logs `organization/users:invite-email-in-use` and returns a 409 that names the case. Superseded the same day by → **(3) internal-domain membership + promote-on-invite** (`e38ed28`). Root cause of the original confusion: `User.role` is a single value and "registrant" was modeled as a *role* (org-null), so one person couldn't be both staff and an attendee. Fix per the owner's rule *"anyone on `@meetingmindsdubai.com` is us"*: [src/lib/internal-domains.ts](src/lib/internal-domains.ts) `isInternalEmail()`; public registration attaches the **event's org** to a new REGISTRANT when the email is internal (external attendees stay org-null); the Settings → Users GET filters to `TEAM_ROLES` so org-bound registrants don't show as staff; and the invite **promotes** an existing org-independent (or org-bound non-team) account — attaching the org + setting the invited team role in place, keeping its password + registrations — instead of blocking. A different org's user is still refused. `/my-registration` is session-scoped (not role-gated), so a promoted staff member keeps their own registrations. Real case: inviting `zaid@meetingmindsdubai.com` (a REGISTRANT with 4 registrations) as Onsite Staff now promotes his account rather than 409'ing. **Follow-on (same day):** two internal-domain tiers — `meetingmindsdubai.com` (real mailboxes) now requires **email verification** before org-attach (created org-null at registration → verify link → `emailVerified` + org attached; new [src/lib/email-verification.ts](src/lib/email-verification.ts), [/verify-email page](src/app/verify-email/page.tsx), `POST /api/auth/verify-email`), while `meetingmindsexperts.com` + `meetingmindsgroup.com` are **temp-account** domains attached immediately with NO verification (admins delete those accounts when done). Verification gates **only** internal/org status — registration still works, and an admin invite/promote bypasses it. **Still deferred:** backfilling org onto already-existing internal registrants. Tests across the arc (denyReviewer ONSITE allow-list, internal-domain tiers, isTeamRole). Verified: tsc 0, eslint 0, vitest 1583, build 0.

- **Communications bulk-email filter correctness pass (June 16, 2026)** — Two rounds fixing the registrations/Communications bulk-email filters. **Round 1 — payment filter was silently dropped on "Email All" (`26f8c50`).** The registrations list applies its **Payment Status** filter to the visible rows + the recipient count, but the `BulkEmailDialog` mount passed `statusFilter` + `ticketTypeFilter` and **omitted `paymentStatusFilter`** — so the dialog's payment control defaulted to "all" and an "Email All" send went to every registration matching status/ticket, ignoring payment entirely (backend filtering was always correct; this was a UI wiring gap). [registrations/page.tsx](src/app/%28dashboard%29/events/%5BeventId%5D/registrations/page.tsx) now passes `paymentStatusFilter={paymentFilter}`, and [bulk-email-dialog.tsx](src/components/bulk-email-dialog.tsx) re-seeds its `localPaymentFilter` from the prop on every closed→open transition (it previously seeded only on first mount, so reopening after changing the list filter used a stale value). **Round 2 — review of the remaining filter findings (`50e27b6`).** A review of the whole chain (page filters → tiles → dialog payload → backend `where`) surfaced four issues, all on the display/wiring side (backend application was correct + zod-validated): **(#1+#4) misleading recipient count** — the dialog showed the page's *advanced-filter* total even when a workflow tile or the in-dialog payment dropdown targeted a different cohort (*"Send to all 200"* while a tile sent to 30). Fixed with a new optional **`recipientCountFor(filters)`** callback on the dialog: each page hands it a **pure count function over its already-loaded rows**, so "all"-mode sends always show the true number for the current effective filters (`BulkEmailEffectiveFilters` = status/paymentStatus/ticketTypeId/agreementSigned/hasSession/sessionRole). Wired on Communications (registrations + speakers), the registrations list, and the speakers list; selected-mode count unchanged. The list-page count **mirrors SEND semantics** (status+payment+ticket) and deliberately **excludes the free-text search box** (the backend can't filter on it, so counting it would over-report vs the actual send). **(#2) "Welcome Paid" tile silently narrowed** — its badge counted PAID+COMPLIMENTARY+INCLUSIVE but the send was `paymentStatus: "PAID"` only. `paymentStatus` now accepts a **comma-separated multi-value list** → `parsePaymentStatusFilter()` in [bulk-email.ts](src/lib/bulk-email.ts) resolves it to a Prisma `IN`; the tile sends `PAID,COMPLIMENTARY,INCLUSIVE` so **count == send**. The dialog renders a **synthetic Select option** for a multi-value (so the trigger isn't blank); picking a single status overrides it. **(#3) payment dropdowns are enum-driven** — the Communications advanced dropdown + the dialog's both build from `PAYMENT_STATUS_DISPLAY_ORDER` / `PAYMENT_STATUS_LABELS` (from [registration-enums.ts](src/app/%28dashboard%29/events/%5BeventId%5D/registrations/registration-enums.ts)), so UNASSIGNED/PENDING/INCLUSIVE/REFUNDED/FAILED are now selectable (were hardcoded to PAID/UNPAID/COMPLIMENTARY; INCLUSIVE was absent from both). **Tests** +6 (`parsePaymentStatusFilter` single/multi/trim+drop-invalid/empty; schema accepts a comma list; payment-filter prop pass-through). Verified across both rounds: tsc 0, eslint 0, vitest 1570/1570, build 0. Commits `26f8c50` + `50e27b6`.

- **Active custom email templates are now sendable + test-email `{{registrationId}}` is real (June 16, 2026)** — Two bundled fixes to the Communications email flow. **(1) Custom templates were orphaned.** An organizer could create + activate a custom template under Communications → Email Templates, but it never appeared as a sendable option anywhere: the bulk-email dialog and Communications tiles offered a **hardcoded** list of built-in types, and [executeBulkEmail](src/lib/bulk-email.ts)'s `slugMap` threw *"…is not supported"* for any non-default slug. Now a new **`emailType: "template"`** carries the saved template's slug in **`filters.templateSlug`** — riding inside `filters` (the same round-trip trick as `surveyExpiryDays`) so **scheduled** sends reconstruct it from the persisted `ScheduledEmail.filters` JSON with **NO new column and NO worker change**. The shared `bulkEmailSchema` gained a `superRefine` requiring `templateSlug` when `emailType === "template"`, so both the immediate ([emails/bulk](src/app/api/events/%5BeventId%5D/emails/bulk/route.ts)) and schedule ([emails/schedule](src/app/api/events/%5BeventId%5D/emails/schedule/route.ts)) routes reject a malformed payload before persisting a row. Resolution uses `getEventTemplate(eventId, slug)` which returns the row **only when active** — an inactive/missing custom slug **hard-fails with a clear 400** (no system default to fall back to) instead of blasting a batch with an empty body; system slugs keep their default fallback. Renders with the same per-recipient variables as the built-in sends. **UI:** [bulk-email-dialog.tsx](src/components/bulk-email-dialog.tsx) fetches the event's active templates (via `useEmailTemplates`) and adds each custom one as a selectable **"Your saved template"** option (`value = template:<slug>`) for **every** recipient type — so it surfaces in the **Email All** flow on registrations + speakers AND in Communications (the shared dialog). [communications/page.tsx](src/app/%28dashboard%29/events/%5BeventId%5D/communications/page.tsx) also surfaces them as one-click **"Your templates"** tiles under the Registrations + Speakers cards. New **client-safe** [src/lib/email-template-slugs.ts](src/lib/email-template-slugs.ts) classifies system-vs-custom slugs without importing the server-only `email.ts` (a drift vitest asserts the mirror == `DEFAULT_TEMPLATES`). `useBulkEmail`'s stale `emailType`/`filters` types were widened. **(2) Test/preview `{{registrationId}}`** now pulls the most-recent real registration's confirmation number (padded serial, e.g. `007`, else last-8 of the id), **falling back to the static `"9999"`** when the event has no registrations — matching how `eventName`/dates/venue already render real event data via [buildEventPreviewVariables](src/lib/email.ts) (pure-sample `getSamplePreviewVariables` still uses `ABCD1234`). Both the template test/preview POST and the email-preview route now `select` one registration (`id` + `serialId`, most recent). **Tests:** +11 (template-slug drift + classification; `bulkEmailSchema` template-send contract; registrationId real-serial / serial-less / no-registration "9999"). Verified: tsc 0, eslint 0, vitest 1565/1565, build 0. Commits `0dbfc77` (custom-template sendable) + `7300ed4` (registrationId).

- **Public API docs — OpenAPI 3.1 + Scalar at `/api-docs` (June 16, 2026)** — A publicly shareable, interactive REST API reference for the **API-key-authenticated** surface (the read-focused endpoints integrators use to pull event data onto their own website: events, **faculty/speakers**, the **program/sessions**, **registrations**, registration-types, **contacts** CRUD). **Strictly API-key only** — the no-auth public endpoints (`/api/public/*`, which power the registration UI) are deliberately **excluded** (they're UI plumbing, not a published API). **Files:** [src/lib/openapi-spec.ts](src/lib/openapi-spec.ts) (hand-authored OpenAPI 3.1 object — keep in sync with the route handlers when response shapes change) → served **public, no auth** at `GET /api/openapi.json` ([route](src/app/api/openapi.json/route.ts), CORS-open so Postman/SwaggerHub can fetch it) → rendered by **Scalar** at [/api-docs](src/app/api-docs/page.tsx) (`@scalar/api-reference-react`, **self-hosted, no CDN**, `dynamic` `ssr:false` since Scalar is browser-only). Auth documented as the `mmg_`-prefixed org key via `x-api-key` **or** `Authorization: Bearer`. **Creates** for events/speakers/registrations are **session-only** (dashboard) or via **MCP** (JSON-RPC, see [docs/MCP_REFERENCE.md](docs/MCP_REFERENCE.md)) — only contacts is REST-writable, so the doc is read + contacts-CRUD and cross-links MCP for the rest. **Enabling change:** `GET /api/events/[eventId]/sessions` was **session-only**; added API-key (`getOrgContext`) auth so the program is fetchable programmatically (same trust level as the existing speakers/registrations key GETs — org-scoped, admin-issued key, the org's own data). The docs *page* is public to view (sharing is the point); a key is still required to *call* anything. Verified: tsc 0, eslint 0, vitest 1548/1548, build 0 (both routes register). **Runtime render of the Scalar UI is best verified on prod after deploy** (browser-only component).

- **Hybrid events: in-person vs virtual attendance choice (June 12, 2026)** — On `eventType === "HYBRID"` events, registrants choose to attend **at the venue or online**. In-person is unchanged (entry barcode + badge + check-in). **Virtual gets NO barcode/badge**, is **uncapped** (doesn't consume the ticket-type `soldCount`, so a sold-out venue still takes virtual signups), is priced via a **flat per-ticket `virtualPrice`** (`null` ⇒ falls back to the in-person price; pricing tiers apply to in-person only in v1), and its **confirmation email replaces the barcode block with a "joining instructions will be sent" message** (the barcode also self-skips on the null qrCode). **Settled product decisions:** choice shown on HYBRID only; virtual uncapped; virtual priced separately (flat); joining instructions sent **manually via Communications** in v1 (the email just promises them — no automated sender yet). **Schema** (additive migration `20260612000000_add_attendance_mode`, blue-green safe): `enum AttendanceMode { IN_PERSON, VIRTUAL }`, `Registration.attendanceMode` (default IN_PERSON, `@@index([eventId, attendanceMode])`), `TicketType.virtualPrice Decimal?`. **Core logic in [registration-service.ts](src/services/registration-service.ts)** (backs admin REST + MCP): qrCode minted only for in-person; soldCount increment + sold-out guard skipped for virtual; effective price = `virtualPrice ?? price` for virtual; virtual **always** sends the confirmation (even free) so the joining message lands; free-virtual defaults COMPLIMENTARY. **Public path**: the register route ([register/route.ts](src/app/api/public/events/%5Bslug%5D/register/route.ts)) mirrors the same qrCode/soldCount/price logic + skips the sold-out gate for virtual; the public event API exposes `eventType` + `virtualPrice`; the **register form** ([register/[category]/page.tsx](src/app/e/%5Bslug%5D/register/%5Bcategory%5D/page.tsx)) shows an In-Person/Virtual selector (HYBRID only) with mode-aware pricing. **Email** ([email.ts](src/lib/email.ts)): `attendanceMode` param drives the virtual joining-instructions block. **Admin/reporting**: REST POST accepts `attendanceMode`→service; badge generation **excludes virtual** registrations; the registrations list shows a **Virtual** badge. **Tests**: +6 service cases. Verified tsc/eslint/vitest 1546/build all clean. **Follow-on (`957abab`, bump 0.4.9):** wired `attendanceMode` through the three remaining create paths — the **admin full-page Add Registration form** (In-Person/Virtual picker shown only on HYBRID events), **MCP `create_registration`** (validated `attendanceMode` param on executor + tool defs), and **CSV import** (optional `attendanceMode` column; VIRTUAL rows skip capacity/soldCount + get no qrCode; template/hint updated). +2 MCP parity tests (suite 1548). **Still deferred** (tracked in [docs/ROADMAP.md](docs/ROADMAP.md) "Hybrid attendance follow-ups"): the notable one is **admin mode-change qrCode minting** (switching a reg virtual→in-person must lazily mint a qrCode — the one correctness gap); also the quick-add dialog picker, check-in UI hiding, dashboard in/virtual split, registrant-portal mode display, tier-windowed virtual pricing, and gating virtual attendance certificates on Zoom attendance.

- **DDoS/bot hardening: WAF audit + live nginx rate limiting (June 10, 2026)** — Follow-on to the Cloudflare removal. **WAF audit (read-only):** confirmed there is **no AWS WAF** anywhere in the account (`803726282629`) — empty across WAFv2 Regional (ap-south-1 + ap-southeast-1), WAFv2 CloudFront scope, and WAF Classic — and **no ALB/CloudFront** for one to attach to (AWS WAF can't bind to a bare EC2). On-box check (via SSM) found **no ModSecurity** (nginx not built with it), **fail2ban with only an `sshd` jail** (SSH brute-force; does NOT watch HTTP), and **ufw active but open on 22/80/443**. So the prior belief that "a WAF is set up on the EC2" was a mix-up with fail2ban/ufw. **Shipped: nginx per-IP rate limiting** ([deploy/nginx.conf](deploy/nginx.conf), commits `958139c`+`0a6283f`, **applied live on the box**) — `limit_req_zone`/`limit_conn_zone` keyed on `$binary_remote_addr` (the true client IP, since no proxy is in front): `rate=100r/s burst=200 nodelay` on `location /`, `burst=50` on `/api/mcp`, `limit_conn 100` per IP, 429 on exceed; `/_next/static/` + `/stream/` HLS deliberately un-limited. Runs **before** Node and **survives app restarts** (the in-app `checkRateLimit` is in-memory + per-container). Thresholds tuned for the **shared-NAT** case (event attendees behind one venue-WiFi IP) — raise for very large single-NAT crowds. **Note:** the live `/etc/nginx/sites-available/ea-sys` is a stripped Certbot-managed file that has **diverged from the committed `deploy/nginx.conf`** — the box is the source of truth for nginx config; the git file is a reference. **fail2ban nginx jail** ([infra/fail2ban/](infra/fail2ban/README.md), filter + jail + idempotent `setup.sh`) — bans IPs that repeatedly trip the nginx 429 limit (default 100+ in 120s → 30-min ban); complements the existing `sshd` jail; thresholds tuned high for the shared-NAT case; **applied + verified live on the box** (status shows `File list: /var/log/nginx/error.log`). **Gotcha fixed during rollout:** the box's `/etc/fail2ban/jail.d/defaults-debian.conf` sets `backend = systemd` globally, so the jail first read the journal and ignored the nginx file — the jail now forces `backend = auto` to watch `/var/log/nginx/error.log`. Operator office egress IP whitelisted in `ignoreip`. Installer is `bash infra/fail2ban/setup.sh` (not auto-deployed; applied manually via SSM). **Docs:** new [docs/AWS_OPERATIONS.md](docs/AWS_OPERATIONS.md) §4 "Security — DDoS/bot posture" documents the full verified inventory + live nginx limiting (§4.1) + the fail2ban jail (§4.2) + a complete **"adding Cloudflare later"** playbook (§4.3 — the nginx `real_ip` / `set_real_ip_from` approach needs **zero app-code changes**; the SG-lock-must-come-after-proxy ordering; the full change checklist). Also reflected in [docs/HANDOVER.md](docs/HANDOVER.md) (Rate Limiting + Recent Additions) and [docs/SUPPORT_AND_MAINTENANCE.md](docs/SUPPORT_AND_MAINTENANCE.md) §7. Deferred follow-ups: Turnstile on public forms, Redis-backed shared rate limiter.

- **Cloudflare removed everywhere + `getClientIp` spoofing fix (June 10, 2026)** — Decision: **EA-SYS does not use Cloudflare or any CDN/proxy**, for prod *or* the Singapore DR box. DNS points the A record directly at the box's Elastic IP; the origin is directly exposed (nginx → Docker). **Security fix (the important part):** [src/lib/security.ts](src/lib/security.ts) `getClientIp()` previously trusted `CF-Connecting-IP` first, then the **first** `X-Forwarded-For` entry — both **client-spoofable on a directly-exposed origin**, so an attacker could send a forged header to get a different rate-limit key per request and **bypass IP rate limiting entirely**. Now it prefers nginx's `X-Real-IP` (set to `$remote_addr`, the real socket peer, overwriting any client value), falls back to the **last** `X-Forwarded-For` entry (nginx appends the real peer via `$proxy_add_x_forwarded_for`; earlier entries are client-controlled), and **never** trusts `CF-Connecting-IP`. Tests assert the secure precedence + two explicit anti-spoofing cases ([__tests__/lib/security.test.ts](__tests__/lib/security.test.ts)). **Docs/infra swept:** [infra/dr](infra/dr) terraform + README reworded (DR SG opens 80/443 via `http_allow_cidrs` default-wide-open, direct DNS, no Cloudflare references); [docs/EC2_HARDENING.html](docs/EC2_HARDENING.html) got a top decision banner + Step 2 marked DROPPED + Step 5 marked REVERTED (the `CF-Connecting-IP` patch it claimed "Done" is exactly what this reverts) + comparison-table rows corrected; minor mentions in `scripts/switch-region.sh` + `docs/MUMBAI_SETUP.md` cleaned. Current DDoS/bot posture (in-app IP rate limiting + fail2ban + nginx, no CDN) lives in [docs/AWS_OPERATIONS.md](docs/AWS_OPERATIONS.md). Verified: tsc 0, eslint 0, vitest 1540/1540, build 0.

(4) The submitter inline edit dialog offered only ORAL/POSTER while the full pages offered all four presentation types — now consistent via the new shared [abstract-enums.ts](src/app/%28dashboard%29/events/%5BeventId%5D/abstracts/abstract-enums.ts) (status colours, label, presentation-type options — exhaustive Prisma-enum-keyed Records). The REST abstracts list returns `assignedReviewerCount` for a row badge. **UI** — new [AbstractReviewersCard](src/components/abstracts/abstract-reviewers-card.tsx) (admin/organizer only — self-hides for submitters via `useSession`): merges the event reviewer pool with this abstract's assignments (and surfaces reviewers explicitly assigned but NOT in the pool), with assign/unassign, a role `Select` (Primary/Secondary/Consulting), a COI `Switch`, and a submission-status badge (score / Submitted / Pending). Mounted on the abstract edit page sidebar AND in a dialog opened from a new "Reviewers" row action (with count badge) on the abstracts list. New hooks `useAbstractReviewers` / `useAssignAbstractReviewer` / `useUnassignAbstractReviewer` in `src/hooks/use-api.ts`. ~~**The COI flag is advisory in v1**~~ **⚠️ SUPERSEDED June 26, 2026:** the COI flag is now **enforcement** — a conflicted reviewer is blocked from submitting (403 `CONFLICT_OF_INTEREST`) on all three submit paths (REST submissions POST, MCP `submit_abstract_review`, MCP `admin_submit_review_on_behalf`); their review can't count toward the decision. (It still doesn't hard-gate *read* access.) **Tests:** shared `meanOverallScore` round-trip + the assign-schema + upsert-decision (no-op vs update) contract in [__tests__/lib/reviewer-access.test.ts](__tests__/lib/reviewer-access.test.ts). Suite 1532 → 1538. Both commits verified: tsc 0, eslint 0, vitest green, `npm run build` 0. MCP tool surface changed (new criteria CRUD + assign upsert) → connected MCP clients should reconnect.

- **Worker connection-pool fix: bigger pool + slower cert poller + P2024 classified (June 10, 2026)** — A 06:05 prod alert (`worker:tick-wrapper-uncaught` + connector `Prisma error`) was a Prisma **P2024** — *"Timed out fetching a new connection from the connection pool (connection limit: 3, timeout: 10s)"* — on `cert-issue`'s advisory-lock acquire `$queryRaw`. **Root cause**: the worker's Prisma pool defaults to `physical_cores × 2 + 1 = 3` (the `t3.large` is 1 physical core × 2 threads; `nproc` reports 2 but Prisma counts *physical*; `DATABASE_URL` set no explicit `connection_limit`), and at the top of a minute several jobs tick **concurrently** on that shared 3-connection pool — `cert-issue` (`* * * * *`) + `scheduled-emails` (`* * * * *`) + `webinar-recordings` (`*/5`, fires at `:05`) — so `cert-issue`'s lock-acquire waited out `pool_timeout` and threw. It **paged** because `classifyPrismaError` didn't recognize the pool-timeout message, so the P1 catch (from the EDBHANDLEREXITED fix) re-threw it to the wrapper-uncaught alert. **Not** caused by the bulk-email jobification (zero bulk activity at the time), but that change does add future worker DB load, making the pool bump worthwhile. **Three fixes**: (1) **`cert-issue` poller `* * * * *` → `*/3 * * * *`** ([worker/jobs/cert-issue.ts](worker/jobs/cert-issue.ts)) — cert issuance is post-event and not latency-critical, so a ~3-min start is fine, and it cuts this job's idle lock-acquire polls + collisions with the every-minute `scheduled-emails` by 3×. Note: `cert-issue` does **no** cert work unless an operator created a `CertificateIssueRun` — the tick is a poller that's a near-no-op (lock acquire + one "any active runs?" query) when idle; the idle poll is what got starved at 06:05, *not* actual cert load. (2) **`classifyPrismaError` now classifies "Timed out fetching a new connection from the connection pool" / `P2024` as retryable** ([src/lib/db.ts](src/lib/db.ts)) → `withJobLock` catches it on the acquire and skips the tick gracefully (warn, retries next tick) instead of paging; same shape as the EDBHANDLEREXITED fix — we'd just missed this message. (3) **Pool bump (env, applied on the box — not in git):** `DATABASE_URL` gained `&connection_limit=10&pool_timeout=15` (pool 3→10, wait-before-P2024 10s→15s). Shared `.env` so **web + worker both widen** (web had the same tight default-3); safe through pgbouncer (multiplexes onto a small set of real Postgres conns; ~20 client conns total, well under the pooler ceiling). `pool_timeout` kept at **15 not 20** so the user-facing web side still fails reasonably fast. **Lever reference** (for next time): `connection_limit` = concurrency headroom — the *primary* fix, but bounded by what the DB/pooler can actually serve (a huge pool just runs more slow queries at once); `pool_timeout` = patience before P2024 — *secondary*; a long value masks under-provisioning and risks slow hangs, so **size the pool, keep the timeout modest**. **Tests**: +2 ([db-error-classifier.test.ts](__tests__/lib/db-error-classifier.test.ts) P2024 case; [advisory-lock.test.ts](__tests__/lib/advisory-lock.test.ts) P1 pool-timeout skip). Suite 1530 → 1532. Verified: tsc 0, eslint 0, vitest 1532/1532, build 0. Commit `e90c989` (code); the `.env` pool bump is operational. Also corrected the stale `connection_limit=1` guidance in [.env.example](.env.example).

- **Schedule/Agenda consistency pass (June 10, 2026)** — A review of the schedule/agenda area surfaced several cross-surface inconsistencies (the same concept validated or rendered differently across REST vs MCP vs dashboard vs public vs the in-app AI Agent). Shipped to `main` in commit `53c8c52` (deployed); package bumped to 0.4.6. **New shared helper** [src/lib/event-time.ts](src/lib/event-time.ts) — isomorphic (server + client, `Intl`-only, safe for `"use client"`) event-timezone helpers: `resolveTimezone` (defaults `Asia/Dubai`), `localDateInTz`, `isSessionWithinEventDates` (local-date comparison in the event TZ), `formatTimeInTz`, `formatDateInTz`, `tzLabel`. Single source of truth so session date-validation and public time rendering all agree. **Fixes:** **(1+7) REST session create+update timezone validation** — [sessions/route.ts](src/app/api/events/%5BeventId%5D/sessions/route.ts) POST + [[sessionId]/route.ts](src/app/api/events/%5BeventId%5D/sessions/%5BsessionId%5D/route.ts) PUT validated "within event dates" with `eventStart.setHours(0,0,0,0)` — i.e. the **server's** timezone (UTC on the box) — so an early-morning (e.g. 1am Dubai = previous UTC day) or late-night boundary session was wrongly rejected, while the MCP path (which used `Intl.DateTimeFormat` in the event TZ) accepted it. Both REST paths now use the shared `isSessionWithinEventDates` (event TZ) + an explicit `endTime > startTime` check, matching MCP. **(3) Dashboard agenda honorifics** — [agenda/page.tsx](src/app/%28dashboard%29/events/%5BeventId%5D/agenda/page.tsx) rendered raw `firstName lastName` and its API omitted `title`, so "Prof. Jane Doe" on public pages showed as "Jane Doe" in the dashboard agenda. Now uses `formatPersonName(title,…)` with `title` added to every session/topic speaker `select` in the sessions routes. **(2+4) Public agenda topics + roles** — the public agenda API ([public/.../agenda/route.ts](src/app/api/public/events/%5Bslug%5D/agenda/route.ts)) didn't `select` topics or session-speaker `role`, and the page's `SessionRow` never rendered them — so the talk-level agenda and Chairperson/Moderator/Panelist labels were invisible on the main public agenda (they showed on the dashboard + single-session page). Now fetched + rendered. The public **single-session** page ([session/[sessionId]/page.tsx](src/app/e/%5Bslug%5D/session/%5BsessionId%5D/page.tsx)) already fetched `role` but never displayed it — now shows a role badge. **(8) Public times in event timezone** — the public agenda, single-session page, and the registration-page agenda preview ([speakers-agenda-preview.tsx](src/components/public/speakers-agenda-preview.tsx)) rendered session times in the **viewer's** local TZ (`date-fns format(new Date(...))`). All three now render in the **event's** timezone via `formatTimeInTz` with a short TZ label (e.g. "11:00 PM GMT+4"), and the public agenda carries a "All times shown in event time (GMT+4)" note. (Two secondary "join opens at…" countdown timestamps on the session page still render viewer-local — intentionally deferred.) **(5) In-app AI Agent session tools** — `update_session`, `add_speaker_to_session`, `remove_speaker_from_session`, `replace_session_speakers`, and `list_live_sessions_now` had executors wired into `SESSION_EXECUTORS`/`TOOL_EXECUTOR_MAP` and were all registered on the MCP HTTP server, but were **missing from `SESSION_TOOL_DEFINITIONS`** — so the in-app agent at `/events/[id]/agent` couldn't discover or call them (n8n/MCP could). Added the 5 tool definitions. **(6) MCP `create_session` parity** — the MCP create executor silently dropped `capacity` and topic `abstractId` that the REST POST persists; both are now wired through the executor, the in-app tool definition, and the MCP registration ([register-mcp-tools.ts](src/lib/agent/register-mcp-tools.ts)). **Aligned + left as-is (confirmed consistent):** cascade deletes, `sortOrder` defaults/ordering, track name+color across surfaces. **Tests:** [__tests__/lib/event-time.test.ts](__tests__/lib/event-time.test.ts) — 9 cases pinning the boundary-day validation (late-night accepted, 1am-Dubai-previous-UTC-day accepted, next/prior day rejected) + formatting. Suite 1521 → 1530. Verified: tsc 0, eslint 0, vitest 1530/1530, build 0; helper logic sanity-checked against the boundary cases.

- **Bulk email immediate-send jobified (enqueue → jobId) + retry logging (June 9, 2026)** — The immediate bulk-send route [/emails/bulk](src/app/api/events/[eventId]/emails/bulk/route.ts) no longer runs `executeBulkEmail` **inline** (N emails + per-recipient agreement-PDF generation inside the HTTP request — unbounded, could time out on a large fan-out). It now **enqueues a `ScheduledEmail` with `scheduledFor = now` and returns 202 `{ jobId, status }`**; the existing scheduled-emails worker (every minute) drains it via the SAME `executeBulkEmail`, and the caller polls the existing Scheduled Emails list. "Send now" therefore means "sends within ~60s" — the request never blocks. Reuses existing job machinery (no new worker; reference patterns are `CertificateIssueRun` + `ScheduledEmail`). **Schema**: `ScheduledEmail.recipientIds String[] @default([])` (migration `20260609130000_add_scheduled_email_recipient_ids`, `ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS` → blue-green safe) so explicitly-selected-recipient sends survive the queue — the worker forwards `recipientIds` to `executeBulkEmail` (empty array → `undefined` → filter-based resolution at fire time). The route drops the inline user lookup (worker reconstructs organizer name+signature from `createdById`) and the at-send admin notification (the worker already emits "Scheduled Email Sent" on completion). **UI**: `useBulkEmail` return type → `{ success, message, queued, jobId, status }`; the bulk-email dialog needed **no change** (it already toasts `result.message` + closes on `result.success`; the message now reads "queued, sending within ~60s", and the send appears in the Scheduled Emails list to track PENDING→PROCESSING→SENT with counts). **MCP `send_bulk_email` still sends inline** (unchanged — jobifying it would change its JSON-RPC return contract for n8n/claude.ai; deferred). **Logging — closed two retry gaps**: `retryCount` is now threaded into the worker's `scheduled-email:sent` (info) + `scheduled-email:send-failed` (error) lines, and a successful manual retry emits `scheduled-email:retried` (info, was audit-only / invisible in `/logs`). So send counts (`total`/`successCount`/`failureCount`), per-recipient + whole-row failures, and retries are all visible in `/logs`. **Behavior change (user-visible)**: "Send now" is no longer instantaneous — queued + delivered within ~60s, tracked under Scheduled Emails. **Tests**: +11 — [scheduled-emails-worker.test.ts](__tests__/lib/scheduled-emails-worker.test.ts) (recipientIds + retryCount passthrough, SENT counts) + [bulk-email-enqueue.test.ts](__tests__/api/bulk-email-enqueue.test.ts) (202+jobId, recipientIds persisted, scheduledFor≈now, auth/denyReviewer/429/400/404 guards). Suite 1508 → 1519. Verified: tsc 0, eslint 0, vitest 1519/1519, build 0. Commit `69c5b7f`. **Doc fix**: corrected user-guide bulk-email rate limit 10 → 20/hr (the dashboard REST flow is 20; MCP `send_bulk_email` remains 10).

- **Worker DB-connection alert fix (P1+P2) + legacy cron cutover + P3 documented (June 9, 2026)** — Two prod alerts fired together — `worker:tick-wrapper-uncaught` (api) and a connector-level `Prisma error` (database) — both tracing to **one routine Supabase pooler dropout** (`EDBHANDLEREXITED` / `Error { kind: Closed }`) on the `webinar-recordings` worker tick. **Root cause**: the `pg_try_advisory_lock` acquire in [worker/lib/advisory-lock.ts](worker/lib/advisory-lock.ts) runs *outside* the job's own try/catch, so a transient connection-closed blip escaped to the scheduler's last-resort catch in [worker/index.ts](worker/index.ts) and paged — a self-healing event surfaced as a crash. Alert 2 is the same event from Prisma's `$on("error")` connector channel ([src/lib/db.ts](src/lib/db.ts)), which fires independently of whether the query promise is caught. **P1** — wrapped the lock-acquire so a *retryable* connection error (classified via the now-exported `classifyPrismaError`) becomes a quiet skip (`return null`, warn-level `worker:lock-acquire-transient-skip`) that retries next tick; non-retryable acquire errors still re-throw. **P2** — added a `DB connection closed` classifier pattern (`EDBHANDLEREXITED` / `kind: Closed` / `connection to database closed`, retryable) AND **gated the connector `$on("error")` log level on the `retryable` flag** (until now `retryable` was metadata that nothing consumed): retryable transients now log at `warn` (still in /logs + Sentry, but **below** the error threshold that fires the SES admin-alert page); non-retryable classified errors (auth, TLS) and unclassified errors stay at `error` and still page. Net effect: routine pooler dropouts stop paging, real DB problems still do, and nothing stops being logged. **Tests**: extended [__tests__/lib/db-error-classifier.test.ts](__tests__/lib/db-error-classifier.test.ts) (capture warn+error, pin the new category + the level-gating) and new [__tests__/lib/advisory-lock.test.ts](__tests__/lib/advisory-lock.test.ts) (acquire→run→unlock, contended skip, P1 transient-skip, non-retryable re-throw). Suite 1499 → 1508. Verified: tsc 0, eslint 0, vitest 1508/1508, `npm run build` 0. **Operational — legacy cron cutover (Phase 4 operational half, done early):** disabled the 5 `/api/cron/*` lines in the Mumbai `ubuntu` crontab (commented, not deleted; backed up to `/home/ubuntu/crontab.backup.2026-06-09.txt`; the 3 DR backup lines — `.env`/uploads/`dr-pg-dump.sh` — untouched), so the `ea-sys-worker` node-cron tier is now the **sole runner** for cert-issue / scheduled-emails / webinar-recordings / webinar-attendance / oauth-cleanup. Route shims stay in code as the rollback handle (revert = re-enable the crontab lines; full code deletion is the remaining Phase 4 step in [docs/WORKER_EXTRACTION_PLAN.md](docs/WORKER_EXTRACTION_PLAN.md)). Verified worker reliable as sole runner post-cutover (stable, `RestartCount=0`, all jobs firing on cadence, zero errors). **P3 (known limitation, NOT fixed — documented):** the worker's `pg_try_advisory_lock` is *session*-scoped, but the worker's Prisma client connects through the Supabase **transaction** pooler (port 6543, `pgbouncer=true`), where per-statement backend reassignment means the lock and its unlock can land on different backends — so the singleton guarantee does **not** actually hold across two concurrent runners. Harmless today (single worker, cron killed) but **must be fixed before running a 2nd worker** (e.g. Singapore DR failover). The durable fix = point the worker at `DIRECT_URL` (session mode, port 5432), which also removes the pooler-recycle that caused the original `EDBHANDLEREXITED`. Caveat block added to [worker/lib/advisory-lock.ts](worker/lib/advisory-lock.ts); the old "session-scoped auto-release" comment was actively misleading and is now corrected.

- **Survey — dashboard shareable link + configurable expiry + Preview fix (June 9, 2026)** — Added an organizer-generated, reusable survey link alongside the existing per-registration bulk-email invite, and fixed the long-broken Preview button. Shipped to `main` in commit `c347b50` (deployed). **Three capabilities:** (1) **Shareable link** — one reusable link the organizer generates from the Survey builder and posts anywhere (email signature, WhatsApp, a slide). Respondents **self-identify by their registered email**, so every response stays tied to a `Registration` — **no `SurveyResponse` schema change**, and the responses dashboard / CSV / aggregate are untouched (they already null-guard registration, and self-identify never produces a null one). (2) **Configurable expiry (3/5/7/10 days)** on both the shareable link and the bulk-email survey-invitation (which previously hardcoded a 7-day TTL). (3) **Preview fix** — the builder's Preview button linked to `?token=preview`, a fake token the public route rejected with *"This survey link is invalid or has already been used"* (the exact symptom an organizer hit). It now opens `?preview=1`, a non-saving preview mode (renders the questions, submit disabled, "responses are not saved" banner). **Storage**: `Event.surveyShareLink Json?` (additive column, migration `20260609120000_add_event_survey_share_link`, `ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS` → blue-green safe). Shape `{ token, expiresAt, createdAt, createdByUserId } | null`. Token is **plaintext** (like `Abstract.managementToken`) so the dashboard can re-display the URL; reaching the form still requires a valid registrant email to submit, so plaintext is acceptable. Lookup is **slug-scoped** (the public URL carries the slug) so no global token index is needed. **New lib** [src/lib/survey/share-link.ts](src/lib/survey/share-link.ts): `surveyExpiryDaysSchema` (the 3/5/7/10 contract, shared by the management route + the bulk-email schema), `generateShareToken`, `buildShareLinkRecord`, `readSurveyShareLink` (defensive JSON parse like `readSurveyConfig`), and `isShareLinkValid` — a **timing-safe** compare (`crypto.timingSafeEqual` with a length guard first so it never throws on a length mismatch; the token check runs BEFORE the expiry check). **Management API** [src/app/api/events/[eventId]/survey/share-link/route.ts](src/app/api/events/%5BeventId%5D/survey/share-link/route.ts): `POST` (generate/regenerate, `denyReviewer` + org-scoped + 20/hr rate-limited + audited; returns `{ url, expiresAt }`) and `DELETE` (disable → `Prisma.JsonNull`, idempotent). The builder reads the current link from the existing `GET /api/events/[eventId]` payload (the new column flows through automatically). **Public route** [src/app/api/public/events/[slug]/survey/route.ts](src/app/api/public/events/%5Bslug%5D/survey/route.ts): added a `?preview=1` GET branch (FIRST — config only, no token, no PII, no DB write) and a `?share=` GET branch (validates the share token + expiry, returns config with no prefill), plus a `?share` POST self-identify path (body `{ share, email, answers }`). Both submit paths now funnel through a shared `finalizeSubmission(req, registration, rawAnswers, deleteTokenHash)` helper so the **existing `?token=` per-registration path is byte-for-byte behavior-identical** (the only difference is the token path passes a hash to delete; the share path passes `null` because the link is reusable). The existing `public-survey-route` test still passes unchanged, confirming the refactor preserved behavior. Share-path registration resolution handles **email→multiple registrations** (prefer an incomplete one, else most-recent; scoped by event slug so no cross-event leak) and a **soft 60s IP dedup** as a secondary guard — the per-registration `@unique` stays the primary dedup; the window is deliberately short so distinct registrants behind one conference-WiFi NAT IP aren't false-blocked. **Bulk-email TTL** [src/lib/bulk-email.ts](src/lib/bulk-email.ts): the survey-invitation token mint now reads `filters.surveyExpiryDays ?? 7`. It rides inside `filters` (not a top-level param) specifically so **scheduled sends honor it too** — the worker reconstructs the send from the persisted `ScheduledEmail.filters` JSON, so a top-level param would have silently fallen back to 7 days on scheduled sends. **UI**: builder [survey/page.tsx](src/app/%28dashboard%29/events/%5BeventId%5D/survey/page.tsx) gains a "Shareable link" card (generate with a 3/5/7/10 expiry dropdown, copy, regenerate, disable) + the one-line Preview href fix; the public form [e/[slug]/survey/page.tsx](src/app/e/%5Bslug%5D/survey/page.tsx) gains preview mode (amber banner + disabled fields/submit) and share mode (a "registered email" step above the questions); the bulk-email dialog [bulk-email-dialog.tsx](src/components/bulk-email-dialog.tsx) gains the 3/5/7/10 "expires in" dropdown shown only for the survey-invitation type, threaded into `filters`. **Tests**: [__tests__/lib/survey-share-link.test.ts](__tests__/lib/survey-share-link.test.ts) — 13 cases covering the expiry enum, record building, and every `isShareLinkValid` branch (valid / none / mismatch / wrong-length-never-throws / empty / expired-at-boundary / token-checked-before-expiry). Suite 1486 → 1499. Verified: tsc 0, eslint 0, vitest 1499/1499, `npm run build` 0. **Note for operators**: a respondent's email must match a non-cancelled registration on that event, and the one-response-per-registration rule still applies (testing the same email twice shows the already-completed state — correct).

- **CloudWatch Logs — fourth observability path live (June 8, 2026)** — All Pino logs now ship from the Mumbai EC2 box to AWS CloudWatch Logs in `ap-south-1`. Joins Sentry (errors), SES admin-alert email (errors), `/logs` Postgres dashboard (everything), and `tail -f` on the host as the fourth + fifth parallel paths. Architecture: CloudWatch agent runs as a systemd service on the host, reads the same Pino-written log files at `/home/ubuntu/ea-sys/logs/{app,error}.log` (mounted as Docker volumes from both web + worker containers), ships them via the EC2 instance role to log groups `ea-sys/app` (30-day retention) and `ea-sys/error` (90-day retention). Chose **host-agent over Docker `awslogs` driver** to preserve `docker logs ea-sys-blue` for emergency SSH-debug, and **over a Pino-direct-to-CloudWatch transport** so the app stays AWS-agnostic + logs survive app crashes (file persists on disk regardless). Same source as the SystemLog Postgres table reads — one Pino write powers four readers. **Setup files**: [infra/cloudwatch/amazon-cloudwatch-agent.json](infra/cloudwatch/amazon-cloudwatch-agent.json) (agent config — schema-strict, no `_comment` fields allowed by the validator), [infra/cloudwatch/setup.sh](infra/cloudwatch/setup.sh) (idempotent install + ACL fix + systemctl enable, runs from `bash infra/cloudwatch/setup.sh` on the box), [infra/cloudwatch/README.md](infra/cloudwatch/README.md) (operator runbook with §1 architecture / §2 setup / §3 optional alarm pipeline / §4 troubleshooting / §5 layer comparison). **Two debug-cycle gotchas surfaced during initial deploy, both fixed in setup.sh**: (1) CloudWatch agent's JSON Schema validator rejects unknown properties — `_comment` fields I'd added for inline docs failed phase-1 validation with `Additional property _comment is not allowed`. Stripped to schema-only JSON; docs moved to README. (2) `cwagent` user can't read log files even though they're mode `0644` because `/home/ubuntu` is `0700` on Ubuntu default — world-readable files inside a non-traversable parent are functionally unreadable. Fix uses ACLs (`setfacl -m u:cwagent:rx /home/ubuntu /home/ubuntu/ea-sys /home/ubuntu/ea-sys/logs` + `setfacl -d -m u:cwagent:r /home/ubuntu/ea-sys/logs` for default ACL on rotated files). Surgical — doesn't loosen `/home/ubuntu` for other system users. **Setup script auto-installs `acl` package** if missing (Ubuntu LTS images usually ship it but the AMI on the Mumbai box didn't, surfaced during initial deploy). **Useful CloudWatch Insights queries**: `fields @timestamp, level, module, msg | filter level >= 50 | sort @timestamp desc | limit 50` (last 50 errors), `fields module | filter level >= 50 | stats count() by module | sort count desc` (error count by source), `fields @timestamp, msg, durationMs | filter msg like /cron:tick/ and durationMs > 100 | sort durationMs desc` (slowest cron ticks), `fields awsErrorName, to.0, subject | filter awsErrorName != "" | stats count() by awsErrorName` (email failures by AWS error code — the Jan 5 webinar `MessageRejected` would have surfaced here in seconds). **Cost**: ~50-200 MB/month log volume = well under $1/month at AWS pricing. **What's not done**: the optional alarm pipeline (SNS topic + email subscription + metric filter on `{ $.level >= 50 }` + alarm on "5 errors in 5 minutes") is fully documented in `infra/cloudwatch/README.md §3` but not executed — pick it up if the existing per-error SES admin-alert feels too noisy or you want an aggregate-rate signal. Operator one-time prereq: attach AWS-managed `CloudWatchAgentServerPolicy` to `ea-sys-mumbai-ec2-role` instance role.

- **Background worker tier — node-cron Node service alongside Next.js web (June 4, 2026)** — Cron-driven jobs (cert renderer, scheduled emails, webinar recordings + attendance, MCP OAuth cleanup) now run in a dedicated Node process in its own Docker container (`ea-sys-worker`) alongside the existing blue/green Next.js web containers on the same EC2 box. Sibling, not microservice — shares the same Postgres, same `.env`, same `public/uploads` volume, same `logs` volume, same Docker `web` network. Closes the "request/response shape mismatch + CPU isolation" gap I flagged in the earlier "would I still pick Next.js" reflection — workers no longer compete with dashboard latency on the same Node event loop. Plan-of-record at [docs/WORKER_EXTRACTION_PLAN.md](docs/WORKER_EXTRACTION_PLAN.md) covers the full architecture + 4-phase migration. **Phase 1** (`dcadc44`): extracted the bodies of 4 `/api/cron/*` route handlers into shared `runTick()` functions under `src/lib/{scheduled-emails,webinar-recordings,webinar-attendance,mcp-oauth-cleanup}-worker.ts` — pure refactor, behavior unchanged, routes became thin shims (auth + delegate). The cert worker (`src/lib/certificates/issue-worker.ts → tickAllRuns()`) was already in shape from earlier. **Phase 2** (`0350592`): built the worker process — 15 new files. `worker/index.ts` bootstraps a `node-cron` scheduler registering all 5 jobs at their natural cadences (cert-issue + scheduled-emails every minute, webinar-recordings every 5 min, webinar-attendance every 10 min, oauth-cleanup hourly at :00). Each `worker/jobs/*.ts` is a ~20-line shim wrapping the matching `runTick()` in `withJobLock(jobId, name, fn)` + try/catch. `worker/lib/advisory-lock.ts` uses `pg_try_advisory_lock(jobId)` for singleton enforcement — session-scoped, so a crashed worker auto-releases at connection close. `worker/lib/health-server.ts` exposes `GET /health` on port 3099 returning `{ok, uptimeSeconds, lastTickAt, shuttingDown}` for Docker's healthcheck. `worker/lib/shutdown.ts` traps SIGTERM/SIGINT, drains in-flight ticks with a 25s timeout (Docker grants 30s grace before SIGKILL), then `Prisma.$disconnect` + exit 0. **The advisory lock is the key safety property**: both the legacy `/api/cron/*` routes AND the worker drain the same job queues during the dual-write window (Phase 3); whichever path grabs the lock per tick does the work, the other politely skips with `worker:skip-tick-locked`. Same primitive also makes the Singapore DR fail-over case safe — Mumbai web + Mumbai worker + Singapore worker can all be up without double-processing. **Phase 2.5** (`8672b4f`): added two public-facing health endpoints — `/health` is a shorter alias for `/api/health` (same handler via re-export, matches what external monitors like Uptime Robot / Route 53 default to); `/worker/health` is a Next.js-side proxy to the worker container's internal `:3099/health` via Docker DNS (`ea-sys-worker:3099`). The worker's port 3099 is NOT published externally — this proxy is the only public surface for worker state. Returns 503 on unreachable/timeout (2s ceiling)/shutting-down. `WORKER_HEALTH_URL` env override for local dev. **Dockerfile.worker**: multi-stage (`node:24-slim` base), copies `src/` wholesale because worker libs transitively import other parts of `src/`; runtime is `npx tsx worker/index.ts` (tsx moved from devDeps to deps so production has it; no separate TS-compile step — tsx handles `tsconfig.json` paths directly so `@/lib/*` resolves at runtime). `docker-compose.prod.yml` gains the `ea-sys-worker` service: same `env_file`, same `public/uploads` + `logs` mounts as the web containers, healthcheck every 30s with 3-retry restart. **Worker logs flow through the same Pino logger as the web app** — the `apiLogger` writes to stdout (Docker captures) + `/app/logs/app.log` (mounted to `./logs` on host, shared with web container) + `SystemLog` Postgres table (the same table the dashboard's `/logs` viewer reads). So all worker activity is searchable from the dashboard with no SSH: open `/logs`, pick `source=database`, search `worker:` to filter. Useful log keys: `worker:started` (boot), `worker:tick-start` / `worker:tick-end` (debug-level per-tick), `worker:skip-tick-locked` (healthy lock-contention signal), `worker:tick-uncaught` (caught at the job's try/catch), `worker:tick-wrapper-uncaught` (caught at the scheduler wrapper — should be 0), `worker:shutdown-start` → `worker:shutdown-complete`, `worker:advisory-unlock-failed` (DB connection died before unlock; session-close cleanup will release anyway). **Decisions locked at plan-time**: Q1 same repo with new `worker/` folder + shared root `package.json` (over monorepo workspaces or separate repo — easier revert, no cross-repo coordination), Q2 `node-cron` for scheduling (over `bree` or BullMQ — minimal, no Redis dependency, job state already lives in Postgres tables), Q3 dual-write window ~1 week (over hard cut — easy rollback if worker has unforeseen issues). New deps: `node-cron@4.2.1`, `@types/node-cron`. `tsx` moved from devDeps to deps. Smoke-tested locally: `npx tsx worker/index.ts` boots, registers 5 schedules, `curl localhost:3099/health` returns 200 with the expected shape, SIGTERM triggers graceful shutdown logs. Verified across both phases: tsc + lint + 1357/1357 vitest + build clean. **Phase 3 is the watch window** — both paths fire in parallel for ~1 week; healthy state shows `worker:tick-end` keys at expected cadences AND occasional `worker:skip-tick-locked` AND `/worker/health` 200s with updating `lastTickAt` timestamps. **Phase 4 cut-over** scheduled ~June 11: remove the 5 cron lines from Mumbai crontab, delete the thin-shim route handlers in `src/app/api/cron/`, deploy. Worker becomes the only path. Rollback procedure documented in [docs/WORKER_EXTRACTION_PLAN.md §11](docs/WORKER_EXTRACTION_PLAN.md). Operator quick-reference at [worker/README.md](worker/README.md) covers all 3 healthcheck paths (public proxy, docker exec, docker inspect), all 3 log views (dashboard `/logs`, `docker logs`, file tail), and the "adding a new job" playbook.

- **Certificates — operator-feedback round + independent review (June 3, 2026)** — Four pieces of organizer feedback shipped behind a planning round, then an independent review-agent pass closed 4 HIGHs in-band. Commits `0c56c9a` (implementation, 11 files, +1264 LOC) → `1e9801a` (tests, +737 LOC, 24 unit + 8 e2e cases) → `58168b4` (4 HIGHs from the review). **The four features**: (1) **Canvas editor undo + Y-axis arrow nudge.** Commit-point undo (one step per drag-end / resize-end / add / delete / duplicate / textarea-focus / format change), Cmd/Ctrl+Z + Cmd/Ctrl+Shift+Z + Cmd/Ctrl+Y bindings on the editor wrapper (tabIndex=0, outline-none), stack depth 30 per-side, toolbar buttons mirror the shortcuts and disable on empty. Arrow nudge: Up/Down moves selected box Y by 1pt, Shift+Up/Down by 10pt, bounds-clamped, only when canvas is focused (not in a textarea), consecutive presses within 500ms coalesce into one undo step so holding the key doesn't fill the stack. Y-axis only per organizer's explicit request; X/W/H are direct-input via the side panel. (2) **`IssuedCertificate.lastResentAt` + `resendCount` columns.** Migration `20260603120000_add_certificate_resend_tracking` (additive). Distinct from existing `lastReprintedAt`/`reprintCount` — reprint re-renders the PDF, resend re-fires the delivery email reusing the existing pdfUrl. (3) **Resend route + listing route + IssuedCertificatesCard.** `GET /api/events/[eventId]/certificates/issued?registrationId=…` or `?speakerId=…` returns per-recipient cert rows (template name, serial, issuedAt, lastResentAt, resendCount, emailedAt from linked run item). `POST /api/events/[eventId]/certificates/issued/[certificateId]/resend` re-fires the delivery email reusing the existing pdfUrl + the cover-email snapshot from the original `CertificateIssueRun` row (replay fidelity — NOT the latest template defaults). Falls back to system default for legacy certs without a run snapshot. 30/hr/user rate limit. Bumps counter ATOMICALLY AFTER the SES send succeeds (failed sends do NOT poison the counter — next click is the same operation, not a misleading "second resend"). Refuses on revoked (409 CERT_REVOKED), un-rendered (409 PDF_NOT_RENDERED), and missing PDF (409 PDF_MISSING with the cross-machine local-storage hint). [src/components/certificates/issued-certificates-card.tsx](src/components/certificates/issued-certificates-card.tsx) mounts above the EmailLogCard on both the registration detail sheet (Activity tab) AND the speaker detail page (speaker page also gets an EmailLogCard for the first time as a bonus). Each cert row: type badge (ATTENDANCE blue, APPRECIATION amber), template name, serial (monospace), issued/sent dates, resend pill if `resendCount > 0`, Download + Resend buttons. Resend opens a confirm dialog labeled with recipient + previous-resend-history; on success toasts the **total** send count ("now sent N times total") so operators don't conflate "resent N times" with "this cert was only ever sent N times". (4) **EmailLogCard "Cert" pill.** Both the cron worker AND the new resend route thread `templateSlug: "certificate-delivery"` through `logContext`, so a small amber `<Award>` pill renders next to the subject on any cert-delivery row regardless of code path. **Independent review (in commit `58168b4`)** closed 4 HIGHs: **H1 atomic primary-query binding** — folded `eventId` into the resend route's `where` clause so a future refactor can't drop the cross-event-within-same-org guard (the GET list route already used this model; we now mirror). **H2 path-traversal + SSRF allowlist in `loadPdfBytes`** — local-path branch `path.resolve()` + assert prefix is `public/uploads/certificates/` (trailing sep so `certificates-evil/` can't slip past); remote branch must be https + hostname matches `*.supabase.co` allowlist. Each rejection now logs distinctly (`pdf-path-traversal`, `pdf-invalid-url`, `pdf-non-https`, `pdf-host-disallowed`, `pdf-fetch-failed`) so an engineer scanning `/logs` knows WHY a 409 PDF_MISSING fired without reading the error string. **H3 setState updater purity in undo/redo** — the previous `setUndoStack(stack => { setRedoStack(...); onChange(...); ... })` mutated other state + called the parent's onChange inside the updater; React 18+ StrictMode (default in Next 16) double-invokes updaters so the side effects fired twice per undo in dev, intermittently mis-syncing the redo stack. Restructured to read both stacks synchronously, set both, call onChange once — all in same tick (React batches the two setStates). **H4 toast wording** — `totalSent = resendCount + 1` so "now sent N times total" disambiguates against the row pill ("Resent N times") and what the EmailHistory shows (N+1 rows). **Tests**: 1352 → 1357 (+5 H1/H2 cases: cross-event 404, path-traversal `/uploads/../etc/passwd`, wrong-prefix `/uploads/photos/`, non-allowlisted host, supabase.co happy path). 8 e2e API-contract scenarios in `e2e/certificates-resend.spec.ts`. UI-level coverage of the resend button intentionally deferred until the e2e seed gains an `IssuedCertificate` row (today the seed doesn't issue certs because that requires the cron worker, which has its own unit suite). **Deferred review findings** (7 MEDIUMs + 7 LOWs) tracked in [docs/ROADMAP.md](docs/ROADMAP.md) §"Certificates — operator-feedback round, deferred review findings (June 3, 2026)" — none blocks deploy, each independently shippable, picked up when an operator hits a related issue. The most notable deferred ones: `abstractTitle` token not HTML-escaped in cert email body (pre-existing, inherited by resend route), confirm dialog state leak on Escape mid-mutation, `handleNudgeY` closure re-allocation while holding arrow key, EmailLogCard pill baseline misalignment. Decisions locked at plan-time: commit-point undo (not keystroke), Y-axis only (not X/Y), snapshot cover email from original run (not latest template), dedicated "Certificates" card placement (not inlined in Email History). Verified: tsc + lint + 1357/1357 vitest + build clean.

- **Disaster recovery — Singapore S3 bucket now mirrors uploads + env + Postgres dumps (June 3, 2026)** — Closed the last open DR gap from `docs/EC2_HARDENING.html` §"Gaps still open". Three independent backup streams now land in `s3://ea-sys-dr-singapore/` (customer-managed KMS encryption, S3 versioning on): `uploads/` (hourly mirror of `/home/ubuntu/ea-sys/public/uploads/`, RPO 60 min), `env/{YYYY-MM-DD}.env` (daily 21:00 UTC, RPO 24h, was already running), and now `db/{YYYY}/{MM}/{DD-HH}-mumbai.dump` (daily 23:00 UTC `pg_dump -Fc --schema=public`, RPO 24h — tunable to 12h by adding `11,` to the cron expression, scripts unchanged). S3 lifecycle: `db/` expires 30 days from creation; `uploads/` + `env/` kept indefinitely. **New scripts**: [scripts/dr-pg-dump.sh](scripts/dr-pg-dump.sh) — parses `DIRECT_URL` from `.env` without `source`-ing (defense against `.env`-as-shell), auto-installs `postgresql-client-17` idempotently on first run, sanity-checks dump size ≥ 100 KB (so silent pg_dump empty-file failures surface as exit 2), failure trap writes structured JSON log line + fires SES alert email (`alerts@meetingmindsexperts.com` → `krishna@meetingmindsdubai.com`) + cleans `/tmp` + propagates exit code, all config env-overridable for testability. [scripts/dr-restore-drill.sh](scripts/dr-restore-drill.sh) — quarterly drill (manual, 15 Jul/Oct/Jan/Apr), spins ephemeral `postgres:17` in Docker on port 55432, drops the auto-created `public` schema in scratch DB so the dump's own `CREATE SCHEMA public` doesn't collide on `pg_restore --exit-on-error`, downloads the latest dump from S3, `pg_restore --jobs=4 --exit-on-error`, then row counts on 9 critical tables (Event, Registration, IssuedCertificate, Payment, EmailLog, Speaker, Abstract, CertificateTemplate, AuditLog). **Three verified gotchas, all worth knowing about for the next operator**: (1) **Supabase is on PostgreSQL 17, not 15** — PG 17 isn't in Ubuntu Noble (24.04) default repos, needs the PGDG repo first; the scripts default `PG_VERSION=17` and `PG_IMAGE=postgres:17` accordingly, both env-overridable for future upgrades. (2) **`pg_dump --schema=public` is mandatory** — Supabase auto-creates platform schemas (`auth`, `storage`, `realtime`, `graphql_public`, `vault`, `pgsodium`, `_realtime`, `extensions`) referencing proprietary extensions like `supabase_vault` that vanilla `postgres:17` doesn't have; a full-schema dump fails to restore with `extension "supabase_vault" is not available`. EA-SYS uses none of those platform features (NextAuth not Supabase Auth, `STORAGE_PROVIDER=local` not Supabase Storage, no Realtime/GraphQL/Vault) so `--schema=public` captures everything we actually need AND keeps the dump portable to any vanilla PG 17 (RDS, Crunchy, fresh Supabase, the scratch Docker drill) — a real DR advantage vs being locked into Supabase as the only restore target. (3) **Scratch container needs `DROP SCHEMA public CASCADE` before `pg_restore`** — because `pg_dump --schema=public` includes its own `CREATE SCHEMA public` statement at the top, and fresh `postgres:17` auto-creates `public` at init, they collide on the very first statement; `dr-restore-drill.sh` drops public right after Postgres becomes ready. **IAM**: `DRBackupToSingapore` inline policy on `ea-sys-mumbai-ec2-role` grants `s3:PutObject` + `s3:GetObject` + `s3:ListBucket` on the bucket, `kms:Encrypt`/`kms:GenerateDataKey`/`kms:Decrypt` on the Singapore KMS key, and `ses:SendEmail`/`ses:SendRawEmail` constrained to the alerts sender address. **Documentation**: [infra/dr/README.md](infra/dr/README.md) is the operator runbook (one-time setup §1-§6 including read-path smoke test, monthly drill, surgical recovery §A-§E for partial losses, promotion runbook for full failover, post-incident return-to-Mumbai, known gaps, cost ~$0.20-0.50/mo for the DB backup line). [infra/dr/POSTGRES_BACKUP_PLAN.md](infra/dr/POSTGRES_BACKUP_PLAN.md) is the design history with decisions Q1-Q3 + §11 "First-run refinement" documenting the `--schema=public` discovery. Decisions locked in: Q1 30-day flat retention from each object's creation date, Q2 alerting = log file + SES email on failure (skipping CloudWatch alarm for v1), Q3 scope = all tables in `public` schema (include `SystemLog` + `EmailLog`, revisit at 6-month checkpoint if dumps exceed 1 GB). Open follow-ups in §7 "deferrals" with explicit re-eval triggers: Supabase PITR (cost $25-50/mo for seconds-precision rollback within 7d — worth it only if business need tightens past 24h RPO), cross-region read replica for sub-minute DB RTO, tiered retention (30d daily + 12w weekly + 12mo monthly), auto-run drill in CI. Verified end-to-end on Mumbai 2026-06-03: dump size 1.06 MB compressed (healthy for early-stage prod, well above 100 KB abort guard), duration ~4s, restore drill green with row counts on all 9 critical tables.

- **In-dashboard docs viewer — ADMIN + SUPER_ADMIN `/admin/docs` (June 3, 2026; access expanded to ADMIN on June 8, 2026)** — Every `.md` / `.html` in the repo is now browseable + searchable from the dashboard sidebar (BookOpen icon, role-gated). Source of truth = the git repo on disk; auto-refreshes on every deploy via `scripts/deploy.sh`'s `git pull`. No DB writes, no Sanity, no in-browser editing — edits go through PR like normal code (planning round's explicit decision). Architecture: [src/lib/docs-fs.ts](src/lib/docs-fs.ts) filesystem walker exports `buildDocsTree()`, `readDocFile(path)`, `searchDocs(query)`.
